class="ng-star-inserted"><!----></gb-ad-banner><!----><div _ngcontent-sc389="" class="boxed-content" style="margin:;border:;"><!----><gb-detail-html _ngcontent-sc389="" class="boxed detail-37517446-html ng-star-inserted" _nghost-sc46=""><h1>Local Scrub Heroes</h1><div class="date">Written on 08/08/2020</div><div class="author"></div><hr class="sep"></gb-detail-html><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-sc389="" class="boxed"><!----></div><gb-detail-html _ngcontent-sc389="" class="boxed detail-37517446-html" _nghost-sc46=""><div class="content"> <div class="texte"> <p>Locals very own Olivia writes about her experiences with her and her family making free scrubs for hospitals in March.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>&nbsp;Back in March a good friend of mine sent out a request for home sewn uniform bags. The requirements were:</p> <p>1. To be able to wash at 60 degrees.</p> <p>2. To fit an NHS uniform in i.e. scrubs or nurses uniform and doctor\'s coat etc.</p> <p>I live just outside of London in the area of Kingston Upon Thames, Covid 19 was being tackled with full force in London and it\'s surrounding boroughs and this was an NHS Matron, a mother and a friend asking for help from us her peers. I can\'t sew, I\'ve tried many times but aside from anything I just don\'t love it. My family however is made up of keen sewers, knitters, crafters. Using the power of whatsapp I contacted my Mum, aunt\'s and sister who all (very quickly I might add) swung into action. From Norfolk,Suffolk, Bedfordshire and Sussex I started receiving bags down here in Kingston. They were measuring, cutting, pinning, stitching and overlocking everyday. As the demand for them in Kingston slowed down, the demand in my family\'s own counties grew so they began to sew and find local groups to work alongside.My Mum is a little bit like me; she has dabbled in knitting, sewing and she can repair something if she really wants to but she knows it is not her skill and her sewing machine is long gone! However, her friend, Cheryl, definitely was on board to help and as the local demand grew we reached out to others to join in and create beautiful bags for the hardworking, brave members of the community who were very much risking their lives everyday at work.</p> <p>Mum\'s home became a sort of "hub", she and my Dad are both at high risk so having already gone through all her bedding, linen and storage of fabric she would leave a box out for fabric donations. Mum would then cut out the patterns and sort the fabrics for the other members of the team to sew/create the bags. They would then drop them back to her box. Then Mum would wash, iron and wrap them with a ribbon and a handwritten card of encouragement. Then back in a different box outside. I would communicate online with those who needed the bags and arrange pick up times.</p> <p>From March to June the team made, packaged, wrote encouraging notes and provided 355 bags for key workers, completely free of charge. Those who made the bags were Cheryl, Gina,Christine and Heather. The bags went to the following localities: St Elizabeth Hospice, Felixstowe Community Hospital Nurses Team, Crescent Road Dental Practice, Grove Road Pharmacy, Grove Court Care Home, Addenbrookes Hospital, Homerton Paramedics London, Felixstowe Community Physio Team and Ipswich Hospitals following departments; Radiography, Cancer Day Care, Outpatients,Bramford, Kirton and Rushmere Wards</p> <p>Thank you to those who donated material, time, effort and love to these creations.</p> <p>Thank you also to my Mum for swinging into action, and finally, to the wonderful members of the community who needed these bags, thank you for your frontline work.</p> <p><em>Written by</em></p> <p><em>Olivia&nbsp; Evans&nbsp;</em></p> </div> <br class="clear"> <div class="photo top" style="text-align:center"> <a href="https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50409030-38918686.jpg?v=1602091782" target="_blank">  </a> </div> <br class="clear"> <div class="photo top" style="text-align:center"> <a href="https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50409030-38918701.jpg?v=1602091816" target="_blank"> <img id="img-50409030-38918701" src="https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50409030-38918701.jpg?v=1602091816" alt="Local Scrub Heroes" title="Local Scrub Heroes"> </a> </div> <br class="clear"> <div class="photo top" style="text-align:center"> <a href="https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50409030-38918705.jpg?v=1602091847" target="_blank"> <img id="img-50409030-38918705" src="https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50409030-38918705.jpg?v=1602091847" alt="Local Scrub Heroes" title="Local Scrub Heroes"> </a> </div> <br class="clear"> Charlie\xe2\x9d\xa4&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-10-11T18:51:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Hi Felixstowe!&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50507671-38967451.jpg?v=1602436200\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-50507671-38967451\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50507671-38967451.jpg?v=1602436200\\&q; alt=\\&q;Kim&s;s Blog: Saying Goodbye to Charlie\xe2\x9d\xa4\\&q; title=\\&q;Kim&s;s Blog: Saying Goodbye to Charlie\xe2\x9d\xa4\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50507671-38967454.jpg?v=1602436233\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-50507671-38967454\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50507671-38967454.jpg?v=1602436234\\&q; alt=\\&q;Kim&s;s Blog: Saying Goodbye to Charlie\xe2\x9d\xa4\\&q; title=\\&q;Kim&s;s Blog: Saying Goodbye to Charlie\xe2\x9d\xa4\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Hi Felixstowe!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The lovely Kim who wrote&a;nbsp; an article for us last week, was so popular and we asked Kim if she would be willing to write a regular blog of her experiences of using creativity to overcome barriers in life. And...she said yes! Hooray!&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Here is Kim&s;s first blog entry :)&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;So this has been such a horrible week for me and my family. Our darling cat, Charlie, sadly passed away very suddenly aged 11. He was such a huge huge part of our family, I\xe2\x80\x99d bought him (and his sister Lola, who passed away 7 years ago) for myself as a birthday present back in October 2009, I\xe2\x80\x99d not long seperated from my then husband and I was getting used to having to share time with our three children and dealing with extended times without them after having been a full time mum for 9 years at that point. The two of them, but especially Charlie, made my house feel less empty. Over time he\xe2\x80\x99s welcomed my partner into \xe2\x80\x98his\xe2\x80\x99 home, we still laugh at his stubborn chaperoning duties, placing himself directly inbetween us on the couch and just refusing to budge, eventually moving to sitting on Nick\xe2\x80\x99s lap to show that he was accepted. He instinctively was very protective of the two children Nick and myself went on to have, putting up with countless hugs and even the odd tail pull with a gentleness that never ceased to amazeme. Over the last couple of years as my youngest daughter Phoebe started showing more and more signs of Autism/ADHD, he developed such a lovely bond with her, always knowing just when she needed him to calm down from a meltdown, just as he always has done with me. He has left a massive hole in our family but we are so grateful for the love he showed us!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;As always, when I\xe2\x80\x99m struggling, I\xe2\x80\x99ve turned to my craft projects to help me to refocus my mind and ground myself, it\xe2\x80\x99s mainly been all about baby blankets most recently so what better way to make you feel better when missing a loved one, than to focus on something so positive as new life! And for me it\xe2\x80\x99s not just one but FOUR baby blankets!! Now, I\xe2\x80\x99ve been able to knit since I was a child, my ever-patient Grandma would spend hours teaching me, as well as correcting my (frequent) mistakes, but for me, knitting is slow, and if I\xe2\x80\x99m not in a great place with my mental health I need my creations to take shape quicker otherwise it isn\xe2\x80\x99t as helpful for calming me (probably because I take on too much for the number of hours in a day, but most crafters are guilty of this). I\xe2\x80\x99d always wanted to learn to crochet, and about 3 years ago, after many many failed attempts, with just the right guidance from a friend, and lots and lots of YouTube videos, I finally taught myself, and since then I do love any excuse to get \xe2\x80\x98hooking\xe2\x80\x99. Three of my dear friends who I have known since they were young teenagers themselves are all due to become first time parents, which is so exciting for them all. Two of the expectant parents are actually brothers, imagine their surprise when breaking their happy news to family, to discover that both their respective partners were due within 3-4 weeks of each other, and for the very excited, soon-to-be-grandma for the first and second time in quick succession. As if that wasn\xe2\x80\x99t enough, at the 20 week scans they discovered one baby was a boy, the other a girl. Now this family aren\xe2\x80\x99t your traditional cutsie frills and \xe2\x80\x98typical\xe2\x80\x99 baby bits. They are much more at home with heavy metal, piercings, tattoos and skulls, so a traditional baby blanket in pastel shades simply wasn\xe2\x80\x99t going to cut it! So, with the help of some YouTube videos on how to crochet a skull applique\xcc\x81, and how to then turn that into a granny square, I came up with some very individual, personal blankets for them to use! These are now finished and will be winging their way to Birmingham very soon when the beautiful little Isabelle makes her appearance!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The third blanket, for another baby girl due in October will have a Harry Potter theme as mum-to-be is a huge huge fan. Finding just the right colours wasn\xe2\x80\x99t easy, but the lovely Sharon at MrsI\xe2\x80\x99s in Trimley was able to help me out, and now that blanket is well on its way.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Then there is a blanket for a lady Nick works with. He sheepishly asked me a few weeks ago if I would mind making her a blanket as a gift. I\xe2\x80\x99m still deciding on what stitch and what colour scheme to go for for that one, so watch this space, as I am sure inspiration will strike me soon!!!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;If there\xe2\x80\x99s a craft that you\xe2\x80\x99ve always wanted to learn, like me with crochet, don\xe2\x80\x99t give up, modern technology is such now that you are bound to find an abundance of \xe2\x80\x98how to\xe2\x80\x99 tutorials on platforms like YouTube, and there\xe2\x80\x99s most likely groups on Facebook for like minded beginners where you can get support and guidance.&l;/p&g; class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Get creative&a;nbsp;for Halloween and carve your way to a top prize!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Families and businesses are being asked to prepare for some pumpkin fun this Halloween whilst supporting a crucial Suffolk charity.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;a href=\\&q;https://www.fsnb.org.uk/\\&q;&g;Fresh Start New Beginnings&l;/a&g; is the county\xe2\x80\x99s only provider of therapeutic services for children and young people who have been victims of sexual abuse, and is launching this fun competition to raise vital funds.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Families and businesses are being asked to carve their most spooky, spectacular or crazy pumpkins ready for Halloween, and to send photos of their creations into the charity.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Entries will cost just \xc2\xa32 and the best 10 creations will be showcased on social media after the judging day held on Halloween .&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The top household entry will win a family ticket for Easton Farm park and the top corporate entry will win a Suffolk Food Hall hamper.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Families and friends are encouraged to get the competition going between households and businesses are asked to get their staff competing for the top prize.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Income and Operations Director Patsy Johnson said: \xe2\x80\x9cWe hope that lots of people will want to get involved with our fun Halloween competition this year.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;\xe2\x80\x9cCoronavirus has impacted on our operations significantly, as we\xe2\x80\x99ve lost the ability to host public events that we depend on for fundraising. Many of our corporate supporters are also reducing their charitable support due to their own struggles as a result of the pandemic.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;\xe2\x80\x9cSadly, we\xe2\x80\x99re also preparing for a surge in demand for our services as children return to school and referrals begin to be made, so we need as much community help as possible in raising funds to help us secure and grow our services.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;\xe2\x80\x9cPlease do get involved, share information with your friends and family, and let\xe2\x80\x99s see some amazing pumpkin creations this Halloween.\xe2\x80\x9d&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Entries are open now and close at midnight on 25th October. Photographs of pumpkin creations should be sent to&l;a href=\\&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/\\&q;&g; hannah@fsnb.org.uk&l;/a&g; or send via our social media and a \xc2\xa32 entry fee can be paid via our website &l;a href=\\&q;http://www.fsnb.org.uk\\&q;&g;www.fsnb.org.uk&l;/a&g; reference pumpkin. A winner will be announced on the &l;a href=\\&q;https://www.facebook.com/freshstartnewbeginnings/\\&q;&g;FSNB Facebook page&l;/a&g; on 31st October 2020.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Written Way before the days of digital cameras and computerphoto editing when you bought a roll of film and had to send it off to be processed. \xc2\xa33.50 for a24 roll and \xc2\xa32.99 to bonus print was 2 weeks pocket money. Now you can get 100 prints for freeon the internet everything has changed the way we treat photography.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Elisha is disabled and has \xe2\x80\x9csensory processing difficulties\xe2\x80\x9d which is a form of autism. It has been caused by a condition called \xe2\x80\x9cChromozone 10p Deletion Syndrome\xe2\x80\x9d meaning she has part of a chromozone missing and can cause autism, epilepsy, hypermobility, dyspraxia and other problems.&a;nbsp;Because of needing extra help and support at school a lot of people have written her off in life with no prospects or chance of getting a job. I wanted to show them that this isn\xe2\x80\x99t true and her creative talents and friendly nature gives different opportunities.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;We regularly work as a team on photoshoots with models (portfolios), families, children and our speciality animals.&a;nbsp;Both of us love all animals and we share camera and posing duties depending on the client\xe2\x80\x99sanimal. Probably our most unusual was a badger. We have regularly photographed dogs,horses, reptiles and occasionally cats.&a;nbsp;At the moment there are certain areas that I photograph on my own because Elisha is 16, but overall we can fill most client\xe2\x80\x99s needs between us. And from the kind comments received we can be quite a \xe2\x80\x9cphotographic duo\xe2\x80\x9d.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Not quite Batman and Robin but we are trying.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;If What a gal... we love her!&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Meet the lovely Kim Lambert, a local lass who uses all kinds of crafts and creativity tocombat stress and anxiety. What a gal... we love her!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;My name is Kim, I\xe2\x80\x99ve always loved anything related to arts and crafts and just generally being creative. I have a cake business based at home, Kim\xe2\x80\x99s Cakes \xe2\x80\x98n\xe2\x80\x99 Cookiesthat I\xe2\x80\x99ve been running since 2012. I find being creative relaxes me, I have a 6yr old with additional needs as well asother children, older and younger. I have my own mental health issues and battle with extreme anxieties too, therefore sometimes just everyday life can be a struggle and very draining, and creating something just helps me no end. It helps me to unwind and refocus, whether it\xe2\x80\x99s working on someone\xe2\x80\x99s cake, crocheting something, sewing (I\xe2\x80\x99ve made countless face coverings throughout lockdown), or my newest hobby of Diamond Painting.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I\xe2\x80\x99ve never been great at drawing or painting, but doing the diamond painting I can create the most beautiful pictures that I can then gift to people. I love how sparkly they are, the sun just catches each individual gem and the whole thing just glistens. Who doesn\xe2\x80\x99t like something super sparkly! It\xe2\x80\x99s actually very simple to do and very therapeutic - in your kits you get the picture which has a tacky finish to hold the gems, the picture is displayed with symbols which you follow to know which colour goes where. You get your packets of gems, your gem tray that you work from and your applicator tool as well as instructions.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I\xe2\x80\x99ve started taking on bigger and bigger projects, and actually approached Matt at 3D Print Hutto create me some storage containers so that I could have more than 1 tray set up at any time. This way, I can work in multiple colours whilst reducing the risk of my kids or cat knocking my trays and spilling the gems everywhere. These are proving invaluable for my latest project which is my biggest yet and is very detailed with over 40 colours.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;If you have mental health issues and haven\xe2\x80\x99t tried Diamond Painting, or any kind of creativity, I can honestly say that it really does help. Give it a go... you never know how much better you might feel.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Kim x&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; ADDED&q;,&q;LOCAL PEOPLE&q;,&q;ARTS, THEATRE &a; MUSIC&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:49775237,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Lis\xe2\x80\x99 Danish Pastries \xe2\x80\x93 Something Sweet from Denmark&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-13T13:05:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Ingredients&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49775237-38610761.jpg?v=1599995273\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49775237-38610761\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49775237-38610761.jpg?v=1599995273\\&q; alt=\\&q;Lis\xe2\x80\x99 Danish Pastries \xe2\x80\x93 Something Sweet from Denmark\\&q; title=\\&q;Lis\xe2\x80\x99 Danish Pastries \xe2\x80\x93 Something Sweet from Denmark\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Ingredients&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Dough:&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;50g fresh yeast&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;250ml milk at room temp&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;250g Lurpak butter&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;125g granulated sugar&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;4 beaten eggs&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1kg strong white flour&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Cinnamon Filling:&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;250g Lurpak butter&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;250g granulated sugar&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;6 tsp ground cinnamon&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Method&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;For Dough:&a;nbsp;&l;/strong&g;Put flour, sugar and butter into a large mixing bowl. Rub in the butter, then add egg and yeast mixture. Gather into a ball and turn out on the table and knead gently. Return to the bowl and cover with cling film or damp cloth. Leave to prove until it has doubled in size either in a warm place or overnight in the fridge.&a;nbsp;&l;em style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;(Note \xe2\x80\x93 the dough takes longer to prove than bread dough).&a;nbsp;&l;/em&g;Knead it again and roll it into shape.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;For the cinnamon filling:&a;nbsp;&l;/strong&g;Roll to approx. 45 cm x 30 cm and spread the filling on leaving a 2.5 cm gap at the top, then roll up as a Swiss roll and divide into 14 (or less) slices (circles). Arrange in groups of 7 on a greased tray or 2 sandwich tins.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;This recipe makes 8 x 7 = 56 individual wheels. Leave to prove again \xe2\x80\x93 20 min approx. Brush with beaten egg, egg yolk, black coffee or cream. Bake in preheated oven \xe2\x80\x93 Mk 6, 200 degrees C or 400 degrees F for 10 to 15 minutes.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;For coating:&a;nbsp;&l;/strong&g;use beaten egg, egg yoke, cold black coffee or cream. After the pastries have been cooked and cooled down decorate with glaze icing (using icing sugar and boiling water only) and cherries cream yeast with milk in a mixing bowl.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Put icing sugar in a bowl, always holding some back. Add tiny amount of boiling water till you get a consistency that you can almost write with. Drizzle over the cooled down pastries or simply dust a little icing sugar over the pastries and decorate with cherries and perhaps Danish flags.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Delicious eaten whilst still warm. Freezes well. If you choose to freeze your pastries, wait to decorate them until you have defrosted and gently heated them up. They will be as good as the first time out of the oven. Great for breakfast, too.&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49775237-38610763.jpg?v=1599995318\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49775237-38610763\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49775237-38610763.jpg?v=1599995318\\&q; alt=\\&q;Lis\xe2\x80\x99 Danish Pastries \xe2\x80\x93 Something Sweet from Denmark\\&q; title=\\&q;Lis\xe2\x80\x99 Danish Pastries \xe2\x80\x93 Something Sweet from Denmark\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/blog/i/49775237/lis-danish-pastries-something-sweet-denmark&q;,&q;images&q;:[{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49775237-38610761&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49775237-38610761.jpg?v=1599995273&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49775237-38610761.jpg?v=1599995273&q;}},{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49775237-38610763&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49775237-38610763.jpg?v=1599995318&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49775237-38610763.jpg?v=1599995318&q;}}],&q;isFeatured&q;:&q;img-49775237-38610761&q;,&q;smallThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/781d6fe914135d42fd8f4b95081d4d46eb23f683/157/93/&q;,&q;thumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/781d6fe914135d42fd8f4b95081d4d46eb23f683/314/196/&q;,&q;originalThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49775237-38610761.jpg?v=1599995273&q;,&q;largeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/781d6fe914135d42fd8f4b95081d4d46eb23f683/750/-1/&q;,&q;xLargeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/781d6fe914135d42fd8f4b95081d4d46eb23f683/1200/-1/&q;,&q;xxLargeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/781d6fe914135d42fd8f4b95081d4d46eb23f683/3200/-1/&q;,&q;latitude&q;:&q;0&q;,&q;longitude&q;:&q;0&q;,&q;subtitle&q;:&q;&q;,&q;isHeadline&q;:0,&q;authorAvatarUrl&q;:&q;&q;,&q;meta&q;:{&q;title&q;:&q;&q;,&q;description&q;:&q;&q;},&q;commentsEnabled&q;:true,&q;commentsPostUrl&q;:&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/apiv3/submitComment/37517446/49775237/?username=[name]&a;comment=[content]&a;email=[email]&q;,&q;commentsUrl&q;:&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/apiv3/getCommentsByItem/37517446/49775237/1/24/&q;,&q;nbcomments&q;:0,&q;subsections&q;:{&q;37517446&q;:[&q;THE as I saw that it became really popular and the second I tried it, I loved it!&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;I have always enjoyed being on or in the water but this summer was the first time I had tried paddle boarding as I saw that it became really popular and the second I tried it, I loved it!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Two of my coastguard friends have their own paddle boarding club in Southend and I then realised that we didn\xe2\x80\x99t have an \xe2\x80\x9cactive\xe2\x80\x9d group in Felixstowe for it! So I set up a page to get everyone in Felixstowe and the surrounding areas so that they could join, learn new skills and meet new people.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;It\xe2\x80\x99s just so much fun to go out when it\xe2\x80\x99s calm. It\xe2\x80\x99s pretty refreshing when you fall off I\xe2\x80\x99ve taken a few photos while I\xe2\x80\x99ve been paddle boarding near the pier and on the River Deben. My favourite is with my puppy Bramble, on his first time paddle boarding with me.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Paddle boarding is really great fun and if you\xe2\x80\x99d like to join our Facebook community, you Captures The Sun In All Its Glory&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-12T11:50:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;The story of my photography now isn\xe2\x80\x99t so much about how I began recently, but more about how did I \xe2\x80\x9ccome back to photography\xe2\x80\x9d. To unbundle that, I had a great SLR camera which I used extensively on the tours that I ran in the East Mediterranean. This was pre-digital and I never kept up with the digital upgrades when I stopped doing the tours. Then along came iPhones and the XR has a great camera built in.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50126694-38773982.jpg?v=1601200663\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-50126694-38773982\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50126694-38773982.jpg?v=1601200665\\&q; alt=\\&q;Local Photographer, Stephen Page, Captures The Sun In All Its Glory\\&q; title=\\&q;Local Photographer, Stephen Page, Captures The Sun In All Its Glory\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;The story of my photography now isn\xe2\x80\x99t so much about how I began recently, but more about how did I \xe2\x80\x9ccome back to photography\xe2\x80\x9d. To unbundle that, I had a great SLR camera which I used extensively on the tours that I ran in the East Mediterranean. This was pre-digital and I never kept up with the digital upgrades when I stopped doing the tours. Then along came iPhones and the XR has a great camera built in.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;My sons sailed (at which they were very successful) so there were a zillion photographs of record. There have been lots of photographs from all over. More recently I have used Felixstowe as a theme.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The reason for the sunrise pictures is very banal. We have a Westie who has been very prone to problems with grass seeds in his paws. So we swapped to beachwalking. By early morning he has his legs crossed and he needs to go. Therefore we rise at 5am with the sun rises at sea from the Manor End. Simples.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I&a;nbsp;have had a very positive reaction to the images I\xe2\x80\x99ve posted on various local Facebook groups and people are commenting on the theme of sunrises which is almost accidental. Where we go from here is partly up to you. Encouraged by the reception, I think I intend to post one a day, not necessarily of a sunrise.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;There are so many quirky and beautiful things to see in Felixstowe all year round, if you just look. Ships, flower baskets, architectural quirks, nature, seasons. Photography is then just a question of pointing the camera at whatever it is. So in a way, photography for me is about saying \xe2\x80\x9chey, take a look at this\xe2\x80\x9d.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Stephen Page&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; Enjoy a interview and stroll with our amazing 102 NHS gal \xf0\x9f\x98\x8a&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-11T15:30:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Today is Joan&s;s final lap!!!!! \xf0\x9f\x91\x8f\xf0\x9f\x91\x8f\xf0\x9f\x91\x8f &q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;Today is Joan&s;s final lap!!!!! \xf0\x9f\x91\x8f\xf0\x9f\x91\x8f\xf0\x9f\x91\x8f &l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;CHECK OUT HER EXCLUSIVE INTERVIEW BELOW!!!&l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87\xe2\xac\x87&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;Joan is an incredible 101-year-old Felixstowe legend who did her bit as an NHS worker, first in Hillingdon Hospital in the 1950s, then in Felixstowe General Hospital as an auxiliary nurse in the outpatient department from 1964 until her retirement in 1978. Forty-two years after leaving Felixstowe General Hospital, Joan walks around Allenby Park to raise money for them. Her goal is to make 102 laps before her upcoming 102nd birthday! &l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;AND TODAY IS NOT ONLY JOAN&s;S 102nd BIRTHDAY, BUT ALSO JOAN&s;S FINAL LAP!!!!&l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;Joan was hoping to raise \xc2\xa31020 for the NHS, but has smashed that target with a whopping \xc2\xa324,548!!! &l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;We were lucky enough to have an exclusive interview with Joan (assisted by her lovely daughter, Diane)... there&s;s nothing like a stroll in the park, and we were honoured to have shared a stroll with Joan. \xf0\x9f\x98\x8a &l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;color:rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.87); font-family:roboto,noto,sans-serif; font-size:15px; white-space:pre-wrap\\&q;&g;It\xe2\x80\x99s been so inspiring seeing Joan has kept on going these past months and is finally near the finish line! Lucy Thompson, Head of School said:&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;The new term has got off to a flying start at SET Maidstone and CaustonSchool. Allstudents have returned and are settling in well to their new, safe environment,within their year-group bubbles. Lucy Thompson, Head of School said:&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;\\&q;I have had a busy start to the year in my new role as Head of School for SET Maidstone and Causton School, ensuring that our school is ready to welcome all our children back safely and making tweaks to ensure that all our \xe2\x80\x98new normal\xe2\x80\x99 systems work well for everyone. We have also been contending with improvements and building work continuing both on and off site, which has been a challenge but our staff have responded with positivity, as ever. Having completed our first full week back in school with all year groups, it has been wonderful to see how well all the children have returned to school. I have every faith that all our children can rise to the challenges that this year will hold, if the past few months have taught us anything, it is that our children and community are capable of achieving whatever we set our minds to.\xe2\x80\x9d&l;/p&g; Here she is to tell us about her musical journey...&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Music is completely my passion. To take it as step further, I have taken myabilities, both in performing and songwriting to Suffolk New College, where Istudy Music Performance. I have performed gigs, along with my classmates,inside and outside of college, notably, the Christmas 2019 performance at St Peter&s;s Church by the Waterfront in Ipswich, where cover versions includedthe iconic \xe2\x80\x98Californication\xe2\x80\x99, originally by the Red Hot Chilli Peppers.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;My taste in music is rather eclectic for someone my age, ranging from 80\xe2\x80\x99spop tunes to Disco and even Punk. However, when composing my original songs, I am drawn to both R&a;amp;B and Rap music. I find that these genres are the best expressions of myself. I am in the process of experimenting my sound and what genre fits me best as a musician.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Some of my music can be listened to and downloaded from all the major music platforms: Spotify, Apple Music, Soundcloud, Deezer, Amazon Music, Itunes and Youtube. Tracks include \xe2\x80\x98Farewell\xe2\x80\x99, \xe2\x80\x98One for Me\xe2\x80\x99, \xe2\x80\x98Our Love\xe2\x80\x99, and\xe2\x80\x98Tell Me\xe2\x80\x99. I try to release new music every couple of months. I have gained alot of confidence over time, which I owe to my college course.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The college studio and accessibilities are unavailable at the moment due to Covid-19, so I have been trying my best to keep up my social media platforms and keep my followers entertained during lockdown. I am looking forward to what my music career brings to me in the next upcoming years. I also hope to do some live gigs locally and also would like to venture further afield to showcase my music abilities.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;If you have any questions, suggestions or would like to follow me, If you love Felixstowe as much as we do, you\xe2\x80\x99re going to love these.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49585972-38528568.jpg?v=1599317352\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49585972-38528568\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49585972-38528568.jpg?v=1599317352\\&q; alt=\\&q;A Bird\xe2\x80\x99s - Eye View of Felixstowe\\&q; title=\\&q;A Bird\xe2\x80\x99s - Eye View of Felixstowe\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Barry Barrett shows us the sights of Felixstowe from above... some stunning shots! If you love Felixstowe as much as we do, you\xe2\x80\x99re going to love these.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I came to live in Felixstowe after I came out of the Army in 1980. I have always been interested photography, but due to working in London, I never had the time to pursue my hobby. I decided to try something different and brought a DJI Mavic 2 pro drone, and then had to get my license and operators ID so I could fly. I proceeded to teach myself how to fly with the help of YouTube. Felixstowe is a lovely place to live with some beautiful scenery. Looking down on Felixstowe really shows what a beautiful town we have, and I love finding different views from the sky to show the town off. I love flying down by the ferry and along the seafront. The town looks good from the air. I have enjoyed this so much I am looking at doing this professionally part time.&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; PERFORMING ONLINE&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-05T11:50:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Having trotted the globe, international Coloratura Soprano, Christina Johnston, moved back to Felixstowe last year. Suffolk born and bred despite her young age, Christina, has addressed audiences all over the U.K., Europe, Asia and South America but she\xe2\x80\x99s always her roots to be in Suffolk.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Having trotted the globe, international Coloratura Soprano, Christina Johnston, moved back to Felixstowe last year. Suffolk born and bred despite her young age, Christina, has addressed audiences all over the U.K., Europe, Asia and South America but she\xe2\x80\x99s always her roots to be in Suffolk.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Originally from Framlingham, Christina grew up with Ed Sheeran and gained her scholarship at a tender age of 17 at The Guildhall School of Music and Drama. She moved to Prague to become a &l;em&g;\xe2\x80\x9cYoung Artist\xe2\x80\x9d&l;/em&g; at the Opera House and made her operatic debut in 2014 at The State Opera, Prague as Queen of the Nightin Mozart\xe2\x80\x99s Die Zauberfl\xc3\xb6te and Adelein Strauss\xe2\x80\x99s Die Fledermaus.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Since then she has performed all over Europe and in Russia as Olympia from Offenbach\xe2\x80\x99s Les Contes D\xe2\x80\x99Hoffmann, stared as Zerlina in Mozart\xe2\x80\x99s Don Giovanni and Katerina Cavellieriin Amadeus with The Prague Shakespeare Company.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;She has sung for Heads of State, most notably regularly singing for President of the Czech Republic, President of the People\xe2\x80\x99s Republic of China and various Presidents of EU Countries. She was personally chosen by President of the People\xe2\x80\x99s Republic of China to sing in China for the end of World War II celebrations which was broadcast all over China. She was chosen by the Ambassador of Israel to sing in Hebrew for the Day of Jerusalem which was broadcast to the Mayor of Jerusalem.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Christina has sung for film scores including, &l;em&g;\xe2\x80\x9cInterlude in Prague\xe2\x80\x9d&a;nbsp;&l;/em&g;and Korean Film&a;nbsp;&l;em&g;\xe2\x80\x9cBattleship Island\xe2\x80\x9d&a;nbsp;&l;/em&g;and sung in Film festival\xe2\x80\x99s for composers including, Joe Hisaishi, JamesHorner, Patrick Doyle, Craig Armstrong, Elliot Goldenthal and Michael Giacchino.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;She released her debut CD \xe2\x80\x9cBlessing\xe2\x80\x9d with The City of Prague Philharmonic Orchestra, and her Christmas EP with Matthew Sheeran (Ed\xe2\x80\x99s brother), was nominated for a 2018 Classic Brit Award and last yearJos\xc3\xa9 Carreraschose her to join him on his Farewell Tour. She was chosen to be the voice and Ambassador of Purple Poppy Appeal, celebrating the animals of the war. The single, A Million Tears, has been backed by Her Majesty the Queen and 52 Commonwealth countries, and will be released this year.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Christina was meant to have her busiest year to date and set to be singing with London Mozart Players in the Last Night of the Proms and making her debut at Snape Maltings in Carmina Burana. However, as with so many artists, coronavirus hit her career hard in March and she lost all her work for the foreseeable future. Despite this set back Christina decided to use the studio in Old Felixstowe to set up a mini concert hall and go online. Every Friday at 7pm, Christina and her husband, (also her manager) Slava, do online streaming concerts from their studio. They set up a GoFundMe page and through kind donations were able to invest in equipment needed to go online every week.&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;blockquote&g;\xe2\x80\x9cIt has been a huge learning curve and something I have enjoyed adapting to. I have found it is far more relaxed and I can interact with the audience watching. We have ha d views from all over the world, from Japan, America to Brazil, Europe and even Uganda and South Africa! I have been overwhelmed with the support and kindness people have shown. It is a lot of hard work each week to do a different concert but I think the a udience really enjoy the interaction as usually on stage I don\xe2\x80\x99t speak with the audience.\xe2\x80\x9d&l;/blockquote&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;If you would like to watch Christina Johnston Live Friday Night Concerts, they are on Facebook live and Youtube every Friday at 7pm.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Tonight is \xe2\x80\x9cSong from Broadway\xe2\x80\x9d&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;a href=\\&q;https://www.facebook.com/TheChristinaJohnston\\&q;&g;https://www.facebook.com/TheChristinaJohnston&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;You can always watch them back too.&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br THEATRE &a; MUSIC&q;,&q;RECENTLY ADDED&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:49531871,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Thoughts on growing up in Felixstowe&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-03T15:25:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Having been born in Felixstowe in 1947 I have fond memories and most of them are about being on the prom or on the beach with my mum and dad. Perhaps your memory plays tricks on you but it always seemed to be \xe2\x80\x98sunny days\xe2\x80\x99.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49531871-38504109.jpg?v=1599139289\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49531871-38504109\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49531871-38504109.jpg?v=1599139289\\&q; alt=\\&q;Thoughts on growing up in Felixstowe\\&q; title=\\&q;Thoughts on growing up in Felixstowe\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Having been born in Felixstowe in 1947 I have fond memories and most of them are about being on the prom or on the beach with my mum and dad. Perhaps your memory plays tricks on you but it always seemed to be \xe2\x80\x98sunny days\xe2\x80\x99.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;People asked me about the \xe2\x80\x9953 floods and I said I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t say anything as Dr Sherlock put me in the Cottage Hospital a few days before the floods came to have my tonsils removed and I was kept in for about 3 weeks. All I saw was the pictures in the papers.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;First school was the Convent of Jesus and Mary on Orwell Road and I remember the vast gardens which now of course have quite a few houses on.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I looked forward to Uncles and Aunties coming to visit as it meant Sunday lunch at either the Alex or the Regal and walk down a leafy Walton Avenue to the Dooley Pub. Spent many an afternoon with a bottle of pop and a bag of crisps.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I have vivid memories of the great yacht pond where we spent evenings and Sunday afternoons quietly sailing our model boats.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I think I knew at an early age that I was destined to join the Army as I recall following the band of, I think the Royal Green Jackets, all along Sea Road to the Barracks at the Port,and being found by one of my Dad\xe2\x80\x99s work colleagues, a Mr Burch, who kindly took me home.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I grew up with two bestfriends that I am still in touch with Tony Lazell and Kevin Banham and we seemed to spend summer school holidays on the beach swimming and admiring the girls. We had little money to spend so all we could do was wander round Charlie Mannings and thought how good it would be one day to be able to afford to ride the Dodgems.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;We seemed to spend a lot of time annoying the council workers in the Spa gardens and running away as fast as possible-I am not sure if this was before or after Mass at St Felix Church.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;We grew older and hopefully wiser and school holidays for me were spent either washing at the Melrose Hotel or washing up and waiting table at the Marlborough Hotel.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The Army beckoned and off I went but always enjoyed my leave back home in Felixstowe and returning when service was completed.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I&a;nbsp;&a;nbsp;joined the world of shipping, as so many of us did in Felixstowe, and at the weekends worked as barman for John Humphreys at the Grand Hotel. Saturday and Sunday, we could be found in our regimental tie and blazer serving in the Garden bar. No jeans or work boots dared enter the heavily carpeted floor. It is now not quite as genteel as I remember.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Eventually marriage and work took my wife and I away but occasional ships brought me back \xe2\x80\x98home\xe2\x80\x99 and in \xe2\x80\x9991 saw us settle in Kesgrave and about the first thing we did after unpacking was to park on Sea Road and walk to the Fludyers and smell the fresh sea air. I have a special memory of The Fludyers as it was where I proposed one New Year\xe2\x80\x99s Eve.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I really believe you must go away and come back to realise just how nice Felixstowe is.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;After some 40+ years in shipping one of my most enjoyable days now is to bus to the View Point and walk the waterline to the Manor Club, then up on the prom and up Convalescent Hill for a cuppa in the \xe2\x80\x98Seniors centre\xe2\x80\x99 in OrwellRoad. Refreshed and down the Spa Gardens to the Fludyers and up to the High Road and the 75,76 or 77 bus back \xe2\x80\x98inland\xe2\x80\x99.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;span style=\\&q;background-color:rgb(247, 249, 250); color:rgb(0, 0, 0); font-family:calibri,serif; font-size:14.04px; white-space:nowrap\\&q;&g;I guess you can say I still like Felixstowe.&l;/span&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;font color=\\&q;#000000\\&q; face=\\&q;calibri, serif\\&q;&g;&l;span style=\\&q;background-color:rgb(247, 249, 250); font-size:14.04px; white-space:nowrap\\&q;&g;Tony Bayley&l;/span&g;&l;/font&g;&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br ADDED&q;,&q;LOCAL HISTORY&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:49499087,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Growing Up With The Grove &q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-09-02T17:55:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Matt Thorpe sent us this truly lovely article. In times of uncertainty, the resilient, reliable continuance of nature can be very comforting. Enjoy the read...&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Matt Thorpe sent us this truly lovely article. In times of uncertainty, the resilient, reliable continuance of nature can be very comforting. Enjoy the read...&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Being Felixstowe born and bred, I always loved The Grove. From picnics as a toddler, riding my BMX round it as a child, playing football as a young man, and walking my pet spaniels around it in my adulthood, I have been a regular visitor my whole life.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Sadly, just before Christmas my last spaniel, Jess, passed away. For the first time in my life I didn\xe2\x80\x99t have a \xe2\x80\x98reason\xe2\x80\x99 to visit this wonderful place. Then in March the coronavirus hit us all, and we were in lockdown. The only respite was that we were allowed one period of exercise a day. Living in Walton, it was clear that my exercise would be walking to the Grove every day.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I was working from home, but every day me and my wife Claire, would visit the Grove. Without the distraction of mad spaniels racing around, chasing squirrels up a tree or digging for moles, I started noticing more sights and sounds. Mostly it was the noisy crows cawing loudly at each other in the treetops. But, one day I heard a low, more insistent chirp. I looked a little way up a tree to see a Great Spotted Woodpecker creeping up the trunk. She had a mouthful of caterpillars, and then I saw a greedy little beak poke out from a hole halfway up the tree. I had found a woodpecker\xe2\x80\x99s nest!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Over the next couple of weeks I would visit every day, and watch from a discrete distance for about 15 minutes as both mum and dad would take it in turns to feed the hungry chicks. I posted some photos on Facebook which garnered a lot of attention. I didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to reveal the location so as not to disturb the fledgling family, but a few people sent me a private message and I would give them directions. I even managed to get my walking - sceptic Mum to the Grove for the first time in years! My three - year - old niece Hannah, would visit with my brother Luke, and she decided that a good name for one of the chicks was Keith!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;It was a real pleasure that I had in some small way helped people connect with nature. One upside of the pandemic has been the resurgence of nature. I truly believe that green spaces and walking among nature is essential for our wellbeing. One day Keith and siblings had gone \xe2\x80\x93 successfully fledged as the circle of life goes round again. Maybe I will see them with their own nest in the Grove one day!&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a &q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/blog/i/49499087/article-385&q;,&q;images&q;:[{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49499087-38488777&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49499087-38488777.jpg?v=1599049252&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49499087-38488777.jpg?v=1599049249&q;}},{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49499087-38488848&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49499087-38488848.jpg?v=1599049593&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49499087-38488848.jpg?v=1599049590&q;}},{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49499087-38488641&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49499087-38488641.jpg?v=1599048804&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49499087-38488641.jpg?v=1599048803&q;}},{&q;id&q;:&q;img-49499087-38488735&q;,&q;url&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49499087-38488735.jpg?v=1599049224&q;,&q;otherImagesUrl&q;:{&q;large&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49499087-38488735.jpg?v=1599049221&q;}}],&q;isFeatured&q;:&q;img-49499087-38488777&q;,&q;smallThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/7c40c2fe09327a357936f72df456d382bee92522/157/93/&q;,&q;thumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/7c40c2fe09327a357936f72df456d382bee92522/314/196/&q;,&q;originalThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49499087-38488777.jpg?v=1599049249&q;,&q;largeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/7c40c2fe09327a357936f72df456d382bee92522/750/-1/&q;,&q;xLargeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/7c40c2fe09327a357936f72df456d382bee92522/1200/-1/&q;,&q;xxLargeThumbnail&q;:&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/resizeapi/7c40c2fe09327a357936f72df456d382bee92522/3200/-1/&q;,&q;latitude&q;:&q;0&q;,& THEATRE &a; MUSIC&q;,&q;LOCAL PEOPLE&q;,&q;RECENTLY ADDED&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:49575088,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Thai Corn Cakes&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-08-28T00:38:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;This scrumptous recipe for corn fritters is a real treat, and it\xe2\x80\x99s also vegetarian plus gluten free (!) made with corn, tofu and a variety of vegetables. The corn fritter batter takes only minutes to make. An easy treat that is terrific as an appetiser, snack or finger food for a party. For a dip, I like to have them with Thai Sweet Chilli Sauce, which now seems to be available in most grocery stores.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49575088-38524001.jpg?v=1599259257\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49575088-38524001\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49575088-38524001.jpg?v=1599259257\\&q; alt=\\&q;Thai Corn Cakes\\&q; title=\\&q;Thai Corn Cakes\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;This scrumptous recipe for corn fritters is a real treat, and it\xe2\x80\x99s also vegetarian plus gluten free (!) made with corn, tofu and a variety of vegetables. The corn fritter batter takes only minutes to make. An easy treat that is terrific as an appetiser, snack or finger food for a party. For a dip, I like to have them with Thai Sweet Chilli Sauce, which now seems to be available in most grocery stores.&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Prep Time: 10 minutes&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Cook Time: 10 minutes&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Makes 12-15 small corn fritters.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Ingredients&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1 cup of rice flour, or scant 1 cup of regular white flour&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1 tsp of baking powder&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;2 tbsp Golden Mountain Sauce or fish sauce&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;2 tbsp soy sauce&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;2 eggs&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1/2 block medium or firm tofu cut into small cubes&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;(1 cup full)&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1 cup of sweetcorn (cut fresh off the cob or frozen)&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;4 spring onions/scallions, sliced&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1 loose cup of fresh chopped coriander&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1/2 diced green pepper&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1 fresh minced red or green chilli or 1/2 tsp cayenne pepper&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1/3 tsp tumeric&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1-2 kaffir lime leaves, snipped into slivers&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;strong style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Method&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Break eggs into large bowl and add the Golden Mountain sauce and soy sauce. Whisk together.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Add tofu, sweetcorn, onion, coriander, green pepper, chilli, tumeric and lime leaves and stir.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Mix separately the baking powder with the flour and add this to the wet mixture. Add salt and extra sauces to taste.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Heat oil in a wok over medium heat (oil must be about 2cm deep). When bubbles begin to rise from the bottom of the wok or the oil begins to \xe2\x80\x9cmove\xe2\x80\x9d across the bottom of the wok, try dropping in a 1/4 tsp of the mixture. If it sizzles and begins to cook the oil is ready. If not, heat the oil for a little longer.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;When the oil is hot enough, drop in the mixture one tablespoon at a time so you have enough room in your wok for the fritters not to touch each other or stick together.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Allow to cook for 1 minute before disturbing \xe2\x80\x93 or until they have a more solid form. Then gently turn them with tongs or a spatula to fry the other side. When golden brown, remove and drain on absorbent towel or paper.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Continue cooking the fritters in batches until all the mixture is used. Serve with your Thai Sweet Chilli Sauce!&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Yum\xe2\x80\xa6 Now enjoy!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em style=\\&q;border:0px; margin:0px; padding:0px; vertical-align:baseline\\&q;&g;Recipe by Detelina&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; photographer Mikaela Rackham, taking place at the Gallery 142 Hamilton Road in Felixstowe.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a &l;p&g;\xe2\x80\x98What\xe2\x80\x99s Left Behind?\xe2\x80\x99 is a solo exhibition by local artist and photographer Mikaela Rackham, taking place at the Gallery 142 Hamilton Road in Felixstowe.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Mikaela has been studying art and photography for many years and teaches both subjects at a local high school. Mikaela is currently completing an MA in photography through Falmouth University and \xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s Left Behind\xe2\x80\x9d exhibits all the work completed during the MA to date as well as some previous work.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The exhibition explores the human condition in relation to nature as well as myths, cultural story-telling and surreal worlds. All the work has been created using nature within Suffolk. The work on display consists of original prints, analogue processes and video installation and intends to create an immersive and reflective experience.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The exhibition runs from the 20th-26th August, and is open daily from 10am\xe2\x80\x934pm, so be sure not to miss it.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;a href=\\&q;http://www.mikaelajaderackham.com\\&q;&g;www.mikaelajaderackham.com Around You&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-08-14T20:07:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Hello Felixstowe, local Pete shares his story and passion for photography,&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50487883-38959840.jpg?v=1602353991\\&q; And Looking Around You\\&q; title=\\&q;Slowing Down And Looking Around You\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Hello Felixstowe, local Pete shares his story and passion for photography,&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Hi, I\xe2\x80\x99m Pete. I was born and raised in Felixstowe and still live here with my wife and children. I am primarily a computer guy but when I can get away from a screen my big passion is photography.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;My journey into photography took a few years having had various levels of digital camera from around 2002 eventually progressing to a DSLR in 2013. Like many photographers, I\xe2\x80\x99m always striving to improve my images and learn new techniques.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Photography for me is something that gets you to slow down and look at the world around you, spot the finer details in the everyday which normally pass us by. It\xe2\x80\x99s a hobby or passion which is different to every person and the sights we see could be seen completely different to someone else.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Felixstowe is a fantastic place for the budding photographer, we have so much variety from the history of Landguard and the hive of activity of the Port through to the peace of the ferry. We have rolling countryside and nature reserves which contrast against the constant comings and goings of the A14.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;This year\xe2\x80\x99s lockdown was unprecedented in it\xe2\x80\x99s affect on the environment and also the spaces that we see every day, which are usually so busy, but for this short period of time sights could be captured in ways we might not see again.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;During the lockdown period I took the opportunity to sit down and skim over the years and years of photos which I\xe2\x80\x99ve had languishing on a hard drive and improve that other side to the photography workflow; post processing. This stage is where you can apply your own style, you can take your photo and make it into something unique.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;These days it\xe2\x80\x99s so easy to get started in photography. Almost everyone already has a capable camera in their hands with the current crop of smartphones. So for anyone looking to get into photography I\xe2\x80\x99d say get out there, try a few things, have a read about composition, you\xe2\x80\x99ll find it\xe2\x80\x99s easier than you think to produce dynamic eye-catching images.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Pete Needs&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a PEOPLE&q;,&q;RECENTLY ADDED&q;,&q;ARTS, THEATRE &a; MUSIC&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:50352890,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Admiring the Views&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-08-14T18:20:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;I have always loved a good view! Think that came from my mum. As kids, driving around the north of Devon on holiday, mum would always say &s;Wow!&s; look at the view!\xe2\x80\x99 Obviously as a child we shrugged it off... but as an adult I now understand the power of a \xe2\x80\x98good view&s;.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50352890-38888038.jpg?v=1601920051\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-50352890-38888038\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/50352890-38888038.jpg?v=1601920053\\&q; alt=\\&q;Admiring the Views\\&q; title=\\&q;Admiring the Views\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;I have always loved a good view! Think that came from my mum. As kids, driving around the north of Devon on holiday, mum would always say &s;Wow!&s; look at the view!\xe2\x80\x99 Obviously as a child we shrugged it off... but as an adult I now understand the power of a \xe2\x80\x98good view&s;.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Coupled with my late dad&s;s love for nature and commentary as we were out and about it sparked a love of the natural world around me. I have always taking snaps, but my love ofphotography has come about through the camera in my pocket! With the birth of my daughter came the desire to &s;capture&s; her and the precious moments that come with a new baby and with her being half Norwegian. Facebook is the ideal place to stay in touch and share those moments with her Viking family as they happen. Having a half decent camera on the mobile makes things so easy. I started taking more and more &s;snaps&s; and then a couple of years ago when phone upgrade time came around it turned into a decision about which one had the best camera functions. Decision made, I was excited about the photography opportunities this now opened up. Actively seeking out the beautiful places around where I live in Ipswich and using our much loved trips to Felixstowe as an excuse for more pictures. Seeking out the best places for sunrises and sunsets led me to either end of Felixstowe&s;s glorious piece of coast. The dip for early mornings, and the Viewing Point and Languard reserve for some delicious sunsets. Cobbolds Point for amazing shapes and water movement and plenty of groynes and interest along the beach.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Photography has become my meditation, it enables me to be present, to &s;see&s;, to become ensconced with how I see and reflect that, to then share with others. I thoroughly enjoy sharing my images and seeing others interpretation of their view on the world through the lense.&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The local photography groups on Facebook are a great source of inspiration and support and a wonderful gallery of talent that you probably wouldn&s;t see otherwise.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;As we get older, inevitably we start to lose the older generation and people around us, and images ofthem become more and more precious so don&s;t be afraid of taking a photo or aselfie capturing that moment withthem with whatever camera you have.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;There seems to be a certain snobbery between mobile phone photography and &s;camera&s;photography but in my eyes the image is &s;seen&s; in the photographer\xe2\x80\x99s eye before it is mechanicallycaptured. I now have a &s;proper&s; camera as well, but still reach in my pocket for myphone camera aswell whilst I get to grips with new technology.Felixstowe will forever be my go to for a dead cert photo opportunity with the Languard areabeing my favourite, there are so many textures, structures, colours and it seems to have anever-changing mood to capture.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Take your photo, whether it&s;s on your pocket camera or a &s;proper&s; camera, share it or don&s;t. See the world your way. If I can help just one person stop, take a breath and see... even if its just for a moment, and be amazed at all the wonder and beauty in front of us then, for me, that is a job well done!&l;/p&g; Views\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/50352890-38888049.jpg?v=1601920085\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-50352890-38888049\\&q; PEOPLE&q;,&q;RECENTLY ADDED&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:50409030,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Local Scrub Heroes&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-08-08T19:22:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Locals very own Olivia writes about her experiences with her and her family making free scrubs for hospitals in March.&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Locals very own Olivia writes about her experiences with her and her family making free scrubs for hospitals in March.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&a;nbsp;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&a;nbsp;Back in March a good friend of mine sent out a request for home sewn uniform bags. The requirements were:&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;1. To be able to wash at 60 degrees.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;2. To fit an NHS uniform in i.e. scrubs or nurses uniform and doctor&s;s coat etc.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I live just outside of London in the area of Kingston Upon Thames, Covid 19 was being tackled with full force in London and it&s;s surrounding boroughs and this was an NHS Matron, a mother and a friend asking for help from us her peers. I can&s;t sew, I&s;ve tried many times but aside from anything I just don&s;t love it. My family however is made up of keen sewers, knitters, crafters. Using the power of whatsapp I contacted my Mum, aunt&s;s and sister who all (very quickly I might add) swung into action. From Norfolk,Suffolk, Bedfordshire and Sussex I started receiving bags down here in Kingston. They were measuring, cutting, pinning, stitching and overlocking everyday. As the demand for them in Kingston slowed down, the demand in my family&s;s own counties grew so they began to sew and find local groups to work alongside.My Mum is a little bit like me; she has dabbled in knitting, sewing and she can repair something if she really wants to but she knows it is not her skill and her sewing machine is long gone! However, her friend, Cheryl, definitely was on board to help and as the local demand grew we reached out to others to join in and create beautiful bags for the hardworking, brave members of the community who were very much risking their lives everyday at work.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Mum&s;s home became a sort of \\&q;hub\\&q;, she and my Dad are both at high risk so having already gone through all her bedding, linen and storage of fabric she would leave a box out for fabric donations. Mum would then cut out the patterns and sort the fabrics for the other members of the team to sew/create the bags. They would then drop them back to her box. Then Mum would wash, iron and wrap them with a ribbon and a handwritten card of encouragement. Then back in a different box outside. I would communicate online with those who needed the bags and arrange pick up times.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;From March to June the team made, packaged, wrote encouraging notes and provided 355 bags for key workers, completely free of charge. Those who made the bags were Cheryl, Gina,Christine and Heather. The bags went to the following localities: St Elizabeth Hospice, Felixstowe Community Hospital Nurses Team, Crescent Road Dental Practice, Grove Road Pharmacy, Grove Court Care Home, Addenbrookes Hospital, Homerton Paramedics London, Felixstowe Community Physio Team and Ipswich Hospitals following departments; Radiography, Cancer Day Care, Outpatients,Bramford, Kirton and Rushmere Wards&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Thank you to those who donated material, time, effort and love to these creations.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Thank you also to my Mum for swinging into action, and finally, to the wonderful members of the community who needed these bags, thank you for your frontline work.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Written by&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;&l;em&g;Olivia&a;nbsp; Evans&a;nbsp;&l;/em&g;&l;/p&g; ame]&a;comment=[content]&a;email=[email]&q;,&q;commentsUrl&q;:&q;https://www.thefelixstoweapp.com/apiv3/getCommentsByItem/37517446/50409030/1/24/&q;,&q;nbcomments&q;:0,&q;subsections&q;:{&q;37517446&q;:[&q;LOCAL PEOPLE&q;,&q;ARTS, THEATRE &a; MUSIC&q;,&q;RECENTLY ADDED&q;]}},{&q;type&q;:&q;article&q;,&q;subtype&q;:&q;mcms&q;,&q;id&q;:49983671,&q;author&q;:&q;&q;,&q;title&q;:&q;Felixstowe Artist Ashley Peck, Painting War Time Aircraft&q;,&q;date&q;:&q;2020-08-04T19:24:00+02:00&q;,&q;leadin&q;:&q;&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;Meet the incredibly talented local artist, Ashley Peck, who took his early fascinationwith aircraft to a whole new level...&q;,&q;content&q;:&q; &l;div class=\\&q;texte\\&q; &g; &l;p&g;Meet the incredibly talented local artist, Ashley Peck, who took his early fascinationwith aircraft to a whole new level...&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I have lived in the Felixstowearea my entire life and remember being fascinated with aircraft from a very early age. My grandfather was a cabinet maker who worked on the DeHavill and Mosquito during World War II and wanting to know more about the aircraft he had helped to maintain waswhat initially sparked my interest in this particular era of aircraft.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;When I was younger, I always enjoyed drawing although I never studied art beyond the age of 14.Upon leaving school, my interest in drawing seemed to slowly wane and before I knew it, it had been a number of years since I had even picked up a pencil. However, after attending the Royal International Air Tattoo in 2016, I felt the urge to draw again and promptly bought a packet of pencils from my local supermarket (the same packet that I have used to sketch out every picture since). I found it frustrating that I could not make the exact colours I wanted and decided to purchase a set of acrylic paints and brushes and &s;give it ago!&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I consider myself to be a self-taught artist as I am learning so much with every picture and still feel that I am a long way from where I want to be with my artwork, although I am now starting to accept that I have time to learn.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;The majority of my work is focused around Royal Air Force aircraft from the Second World War era and I hope that my paintings will go some way towards telling the story of the men and women who built, flew and maintained them. I do occasionally paint modern or commercial aircraft, and feel comfortable trying any mechanical subject.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Over the last couple of years, I have been very fortunate in that I have been able to display my paintings at a small number of events held at local airfields such as Rougham and Monewden as well as Felixstowe\xe2\x80\x99s Art On The Prom in 2018. Meeting people at these events has provided inspiration for more paintings and so the cycle continues.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;Soon I hope to create a series of paintings with a Felixstowe connection to shine a light on the role that Felixstowe and its residents played before, during and after the conflict. If anybody has any stories that they would like to see translated to canvas, I\xe2\x80\x99d love to hear them.&l;/p&g; &l;p&g;I\xe2\x80\x99m on Facebook as &l;a href=\\&q;https://www.facebook.com/A-Peck-Aviation-Art-1674990425873837\\&q;&g;A Peck Aviation Ar t&l;/a&g;and my website is &l;a href=\\&q;http://www.aviationpaintings.co.uk\\&q;&g;www.aviationpaintings.co.uk.&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g; &l;div&g;&a;nbsp;&l;/div&g; &l;div class=\\&q;_1GmxSv9K16\\&q; style=\\&q;position: absolute; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; width: 0px; height: 0px; transform-origin: left top; box-sizing: border-box; color: rgb(0, 0, 0); font-family: system-ui; font-size: 14px; background-color: rgb(247, 249, 250); transform: scale(1);\\&q;&g;&a;nbsp;&l;/div&g; &l;div class=\\&q;_1GmxSv9K16\\&q; style=\\&q;position: absolute; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; width: 0px; height: 0px; transform-origin: left top; box-sizing: border-box; color: rgb(0, 0, 0); font-family: system-ui; font-size: 14px; background-color: rgb(247, 249, 250); transform: scale(1);\\&q;&g;&a;nbsp;&l;/div&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q; style=\\&q;text-align:center\\&q;&g; &l;a href=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/grande/49983671-38709058.jpg?v=1600710994\\&q; target=\\&q;_blank\\&q;&g; &l;img id=\\&q;img-49983671-38709058\\&q; src=\\&q;https://cmsphoto.ww-cdn.com/superstatic/2348751/art/default/49983671-38709058.jpg?v=1600710994\\&q; alt=\\&q;Felixstowe Artist Ashley Peck, Painting War Time Aircraft\\&q; title=\\&q;Felixstowe Artist Ashley Peck, Painting War Time Aircraft\\&q; /&g; &l;/a&g; &l;/div&g; &l;br class=\\&q;clear\\&q; /&g; &l;div class=\\&q;photo top\\&q;
